<B>
	Risk factors

<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Investors should carefully consider the risks and uncertainties described below before making an investment decision. If any of the following risks actually occur, our business, financial condition or operating results could be materially harmed. This could cause the trading price of our common shares to decline, and you may lose all or part of your investment. The items of the following list of risk factors are in no particular order or priority to the Company.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
<U>
	RISKS ASSOCIATED WITH FINANCIAL RESULTS
</U>
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company&#8217;s inability to generate sufficient cash flows from its operations may affect its ability to continue as a going concern.
</B>
	The Company&#8217;s consolidated financial statements have been prepared on a going concern basis, which presumes the realization of assets and the settlement of liabilities in the normal course of operations. The application of the going concern basis is dependent upon the Company having sufficient available cash resources and achieving profitable operations to generate sufficient cash flows to fund continued operations. Should the Company fail to generate sufficient cash flows from operations, it will require additional financing to remain a going concern.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	8
</P>
</DIV>
<BR>
<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage9"></A>
<BR>
<!--$$/PAGE=-->
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_9">
</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE=" PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company&#8217;s inability to accurately forecast its results from quarter-to-quarter may affect its cash resources and result in wide fluctuations in the market price of the Company's stock.
</B>
	The operating results have varied on a quarterly basis in the past and may fluctuate significantly in the future as a result of a variety of factors, many of which are described below. Due to these and other factors, most of which are outside of the Company&#8217;s control, the quarterly revenues and operating results are difficult to forecast. As a result, the Company may not be able to accurately predict its necessary cash expenditures during each quarter or obtain financing in a timely manner to cover any shortfalls. The Company also believes that period-to-period comparisons of its operating results may not be meaningful and one should not rely on any such comparisons as an indication of its future performance.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
<U>
	RISKS ASSOCIATED WITH BUSINESS AND OPERATIONS
</U>
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The Company&#8217;s exposure to business and operation risks includes but is not limited to the following:
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company recognizes the threats posed by operating in an uncertain global economic environment.
</B>
	The uncertain global economy and financial markets continue to limit overall visibility to end markets. This uncertainty may continue to impact our industry, resulting in lower demand for some of the products we manufacture and limiting end-market visibility for our customers. This environment can pose significant risk to our business by impacting demand for our customers&#8217; products, the financial condition of our customers or suppliers, as well as the level of customer satisfaction. A deterioration in economic environment may accelerate the effect of the various risk factors described in this Annual Report, as well as result in other unforeseen events that will impact our business and financial condition.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company cannot be sure it will be able to identify emerging technology and market trends, enhance its existing technologies or develop new technologies in order to effectively compete in the communications industry.
</B>
	The communications industry is characterized by rapid technological changes, short technology and product life cycles, pressure to provide improved solutions at increasingly lower prices and frequent introduction of new technologies and products. To succeed, the Company must be able to control spending and prudently allocate financial resources to optimize value. Also, the Company must identify emerging trends and enhance its existing technologies and develop new technologies and products to meet market requirements. To drive sales, the Company&#8217;s products must meet the needs of existing and potential customers and be competitively priced; additional judgment will need to be exercised if the granting of credit to customers is required to close the transaction. In view of the current difficulty, both in obtaining credit and accessing the capital markets, stewardship of cash continues to be critical to the Company&#8217;s success. Additionally, there must be sufficient interest in and demand for the Company&#8217;s products. If the Company does not develop these new technologies and products in a timely and cost effective manner, or if others develop new technologies ahead of us, the Company may not achieve profitability in the communications industry and may not be able to participate in selling these new technologies or products. While the Company is able to continue to develop products with funding contributions from the Canadian Federal Government through the SADI program; without the SADI program contribution, the Company&#8217;s product development costs would not be sustainable, thereby jeopardizing our ability to maintain product innovation and leadership.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company has customer concentration.
</B>
	A significant portion of the Company&#8217;s revenues have been recognized from a customer. A decline in revenue from the customer on which we are dependent or the loss of a large customer could have a material effect on our financial condition and operating results.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For the year ended December 31, 2015, one customer of the Sinclair Technologies operating segment represented 10% of the Company&#8217;s consolidated revenue (2014 &#8211; 11%, 2013 &#8211; 14%, 2012 &#8211; 11%, 2011 - Nil).
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	9
</P>
</DIV>
<BR>
<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage10"></A>
<BR>
<!--$$/PAGE=-->
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_10">
</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE=" PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	While the Company has been diversifying its customer base, the efforts to date may be insufficient to offset the effects of the quarterly variance of sales and delays associated with selling to the government sector. The Company expects that a majority of the Satellite Communications revenues will continue to be dependent on sales to a small number of customers. The Company also expects that customers will vary from period-to-period as existing customers are under no obligation to continue buying from Norsat.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company cannot be sure that it will be able to compete effectively with its current competitors.
</B>
	The Company&#8217;s markets are intensely competitive. Some competitors have technologies and products that may be more advantageous and compete directly with the Company. Some of these competitors are large, established companies which have significantly greater resources than we do.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Aggressive pricing is a common business dynamic in our markets. Some of our competitors have greater scale as well as a broader service offering than we have. Some of our current or potential competitors may also increase or shift their presence in new lower-cost regions to try to offset the continuous competitive pressure and increasing labor costs, may develop or acquire services comparable or superior to those we develop, combine or merge to form larger competitors, or adapt more quickly than we may to new technologies, evolving industry trends and changing customer requirements.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The Company&#8217;s ability to compete effectively will depend on its ability to increase sales, attract new customers in a timely and cost effective manner and sell these products at competitive prices. The Company is dependent on others for the supply and manufacture of components and products it sells. The Company has outsourced substantially all of the manufacturing of the microwave products it sells. The Company relies on its suppliers to provide components for the production of other products. If either the manufacturers or suppliers cannot deliver products to the Company on time, its revenues and profits will be adversely affected.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company has limited intellectual property protection.
</B>
	The Company&#8217;s success and ability to compete are dependent, in part, upon its proprietary technology, brand and reputation in the marketplace, and customer relationships. While the Company currently holds four patents (US Patents# 6931245; 7218289; 8200150; 8125400) and has applied for patent protection on certain other parts of its technology, it relies primarily on trade secrets and does not have adequate trademark and patent protection on all of its technology. The Company also enters into confidentiality, and non-compete agreements with its employees and limits the access to and distribution of the product design documentation and other proprietary information. The Company cannot be sure that these efforts will deter misappropriation or prevent an unauthorized third party, including former associates and former employees, from obtaining or using information, which it deems to be proprietary. Although the Company believes that its technology does not currently infringe upon patents or trademarks held by others, it cannot be sure that such infringements do not exist or will not exist in the future, particularly as the number of products and competitors in its industry segment grows.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	If the Company experiences rapid growth and does not manage it effectively, profitability may be affected
</B>
	. If our technologies and products achieve widespread acceptance, the Company may experience rapid growth. This growth may require the Company to hire more employees, recruit additional management, improve its financial control systems, and expand and manage the technical, sales and support service operations. The Company will need increased revenues and additional funding to operate these increased activities. If the Company does not manage its growth effectively, its profitability may be impacted.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company depends on its key employees and it cannot be sure that it will be able to keep these employees or hire and train replacements
</B>
	. The Company&#8217;s success depends on the skills, experience and performance of the senior management and other key personnel. While
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	10
</P>
</DIV>
<BR>
<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage11"></A>
<BR>
<!--$$/PAGE=-->
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_11">
</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE=" PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	it offers competitive compensation packages and stock options to attract key employees, the Company does not carry key person insurance on these employees. Highly skilled technical employees and management in the communications industry are in demand and the market for such persons is highly competitive. The Company cannot be sure that it will be able to retain these employees or hire replacements. If the Company does not successfully retain the key personnel or hire and train replacements, it will be unable to develop the new products and technologies necessary to compete in its markets or to effectively manage its business.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company intends to expand its international operations, and thus faces a number of risks including tariffs, export controls and other trade barriers; political and economic instability in foreign markets; and fluctuations in foreign currencies.
</B>
	These external risks may not be under the Company&#8217;s control. Additional human and financial resources may be required for this expansion which the Company may not be able to attract or afford. Failure to expand internationally may impact the Company&#8217;s prospects for revenue growth and profitability.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company may encounter difficulties completing or integrating our acquisitions which could adversely affect its operating results.
</B>
	The Company expects to expand its presence in new end-markets or expand its capabilities, some of which may occur through acquisitions. These transactions may involve acquisitions of entire companies and/or acquisitions of selected assets of companies. Potential difficulties related to our acquisitions include:
</P>
<UL>
<LI>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-LEFT: 4%" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	integrating acquired operations, systems and businesses;
</P>
<LI>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-LEFT: 4%" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	retaining customer, supplier, employee or other business relationships of acquired operations;
</P>
<LI>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-LEFT: 4%" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	addressing unforeseen liabilities of acquired businesses;
</P>
<LI>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-LEFT: 4%" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	limited experience with new technologies; and
</P>
<LI>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-LEFT: 4%" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	not achieving anticipated business volumes.
</P>
</LI>
</UL>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Any of these factors could prevent the Company from realizing the anticipated benefits of an acquisition, including additional revenue, operational synergies and economies of scale. The Company&#8217;s failure to realize the anticipated benefits of acquisitions could adversely affect its business and operating results. The Company&#8217;s acquisition of Sinclair Technologies Holdings Inc. in 2011 has resulted in the recording of a significant amount of goodwill and intangible assets at the time of acquisition. The Company&#8217;s failure to support the carrying value of goodwill and intangible assets in periods subsequent to the acquisitions could require write-downs that adversely affect our financial results.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	In certain instances, the Company sells products which may be subject to export and/or re-export restrictions.
</B>
	The export laws of the governments of Canada and United States apply to products that the Company sells. The United States Department of Commerce, through its Export Administration Regulations, and the Government of Canada, through its Export Controls Division, regulate exports and re-exports of "dual-use" items, i.e., goods, software and technologies with commercial and proliferation/ military applications. In ascertaining whether such items may be subject to export control restrictions, the Company is sometimes forced to rely on information in the specifications of certain components from the manufacturers and vendors. Should this information later prove to be incorrect, the Company may be subjected to penalties and fines. It may also be subjected to penalties and fines should there be a breach in the processes.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company buys components and products which may, in certain instances, be subject to contractual obligations to purchase minimum quantities during a given period, maintain resale records and abide by certain resale restrictions.
</B>
	Failure to fulfil any or all of these may negatively impact liquidity should the Company be forced to take ownership of any un-purchased units. It may also affect the Company&#8217;s ability to continue supplying products as originally specified and thus affect obligations to fulfil orders.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	11
</P>
</DIV>
<BR>
<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage12"></A>
<BR>
<!--$$/PAGE=-->
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_12">
</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE=" PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company may be subject to product liability claims, which are not fully covered by insurance.
</B>
	The manufacture, sale and marketing of our products expose us to the risk of product liability claims. Given the complex nature of our products, the products may contain undetected errors or performance problems may arise. Although the Company&#8217;s products undergo testing prior to release into the market, it is possible that such products may yet still contain errors and performance problems, which are discovered only after commercial introduction. If these defects and errors are discovered after shipment, they could result in a loss of sales revenues, delay in market acceptance, product returns, warranty claims and the loss of a potential market. In addition, components and other products manufactured and distributed by others, which are incorporated into the Company&#8217;s products, may also contain such defects and errors, which could substantially reduce the performance of the products. The Company is also at risk of exposure to potential product liability claims from distributors and end-users for damages resulting from defects in products that it distributes. Although product defects have not been a significant factor, the Company maintains comprehensive general liability insurance which provides limited coverage against claims originating in product failure. The Company cannot be sure that this insurance will be adequate to cover all claims brought against us or that this insurance will continue to be available to us on acceptable terms. If these claims are not fully covered by the Company&#8217;s product liability insurance, they could severely and negatively impact the business liability insurance coverage and the available cash resources. A product liability claim, even one without merit or for which the Company has substantial coverage, could result in significant legal defense costs, thereby increasing the expenses, lowering the earnings and, depending on revenues, potentially resulting in additional losses.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company&#8217;s operations may be disrupted by natural disasters and extreme weather conditions.
</B>
	The Company&#8217;s headquarters is located in the Greater Vancouver region which has, in recent times, been subjected to high winds and extreme weather conditions. While the Company has managed to continue operating through some of these conditions, employee productivity during these periods is negatively impacted.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	Long sales and implementation cycles for the Company&#8217;s products may adversely affect its operating results.
</B>
	The Company&#8217;s customers generally devote substantial time, money and other resources to their purchasing decisions. Typically, the larger the potential sale, the more time, money and other resources will be invested. As a result, it may take many months or a few years after the first contact with a customer before a sale may actually be completed. The Company may invest significant sales and other resources in a potential customer that may not generate revenue for a substantial period of time, if at all. Long sales and implementation cycles may affect the size or timing of the order or even cause it to be cancelled. For example, purchasing decisions may be postponed, or large purchases reduced, during periods of economic uncertainty; the Company or its competitors may announce or introduce new products; or the customer&#8217;s own budget and purchasing needs may change. In addition, long sales and implementation cycles may impact the margins that the Company earns on its products. It may cost the Company more to produce its products by the time the purchasing decision is made due to increased supply costs or currency fluctuations. If these events were to occur, sales of the Company&#8217;s products may be cancelled or delayed, which would reduce its revenue.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	Mergers or other strategic transactions by competitors could weaken the Company&#8217;s competitive position or reduce its revenue.
</B>
	If one or more of our competitors were to merge or partner with another of our competitors, the change in the competitive landscape could adversely affect our ability to compete effectively. Our competitors may also establish or strengthen co-operative relationships with existing or prospective clients, thereby limiting our ability to promote its products and services. Disruptions in the Company&#8217;s business caused by these events could reduce its competitiveness and ultimately its revenue.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	If the Company&#8217;s suppliers do not supply us with a sufficient amount and quality of components at acceptable prices, and in a timely manner, our ability to manufacture the Company&#8217;s products would be harmed and the business would suffer.
</B>
	The Company relies
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	12
</P>
</DIV>
<BR>
<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage13"></A>
<BR>
<!--$$/PAGE=-->
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_13">
</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE=" PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	on third-party suppliers to provide components and product subassemblies. A supplier&#8217;s failure to supply components or product subassemblies in a timely manner, or failure to supply components or product subassemblies that meet the Company&#8217;s quality, quantity or cost requirements, or its inability to obtain substitute sources of these components or product subassemblies in a timely manner or on terms acceptable to the Company, could adversely affect its ability to manufacture or source products. The Company may experience delays in the manufacture or sourcing of products and the business and financial results would suffer if we fail to identify alternate suppliers, or if our supply is interrupted or reduced or if there is a significant increase in cost.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company&#8217;s level of indebtedness and failure to comply with its indebtedness arrangements may adversely affect its business and operations.
</B>
	The Company relies on the availability of indebtedness arrangements with its lenders. The arrangements contain restrictive covenants that limit the Company&#8217;s discretion with respect to certain business matters. These covenants place significant restrictions on the Company&#8217;s ability to pledge or create liens or other encumbrances on its assets. These financial covenants require the Company to meet certain financial ratios and financial condition tests. If the lender was to demand or cancel these facilities, there can be no assurance that the Company&#8217;s assets would be sufficient to repay in full the indebtedness. It is possible that the Company will not have sufficient funds at the time to fund its operations. In addition, there can be no assurance that future borrowings or equity financing will be available to the Company or available on acceptable terms, in an amount sufficient to meet its repayment obligations. In the event that the lending arrangements cannot be refinanced, or if they can only be refinanced on terms that are less favorable than the current terms, the Company&#8217;s business and operations may be adversely affected.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company is subject to the risk of increased income taxes and our ability to successfully defend tax audits could adversely affect our financial condition and financial results.
</B>
	The Company conducts business operations in a number of countries. The Company develops its tax filing positions based upon the anticipated nature and structure of our business and the tax laws, administrative practices and judicial decisions currently in effect in the jurisdictions in which the Company has assets or conducts business, all of which are subject to change or differing interpretations, possibly with retroactive effect. In addition, certain of our subsidiaries provide financing, products and services to, and may from time-to-time undertake certain significant transactions with, other subsidiaries in different jurisdictions. Moreover, several jurisdictions in which the Company operates have tax laws with detailed transfer pricing rules which require that all transactions with non-resident related parties be priced using arm&#8217;s length pricing principles, and that contemporaneous documentation must exist to support such pricing.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The Company is subject to tax audits and reviews by local tax authorities of historical information and our contemporaneous documentation which could result in additional tax expense in future periods relating to prior results. Any such increase in our income tax expense and related interest and penalties could have a significant impact on the Company&#8217;s future earnings and future cash flows.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	Any failure to successfully manage the Company&#8217;s international operations would have a material adverse effect on its financial condition and operating results.
</B>
	The Company has operations in a number of countries, including Canada, United States, United Kingdom and Switzerland. International operations are subject to inherent risks which may adversely affect us, including:
</P>
<UL>
<LI>

<LI>

</P>

<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
<U>
	RISKS ASSOCIATED WITH THE VALUE OF NORSAT SHARES
</U>
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The exercise of the existing outstanding options may substantially dilute the value of the Company&#8217;s common shares
</B>
	. The Company has unlimited number of Common Stock authorized, of which 5,831,658 were outstanding on a post-consolidated basis at March 18, 2016. See Item 10B below for more information. Although the Board of Directors has no present intention to do so, it has the authority, within parameters set by the Toronto Stock Exchange (the &#8220;TSX&#8221;), without action by the shareholders, to issue authorized and unissued shares of Common Stock. Any series of Preferred Stock, if and when established and issued, could also have rights superior to shares of the Company&#8217;s Common Stock, particularly in regard to voting, the payment of dividends and upon liquidation of Norsat.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The current financial market volatility can result in wide fluctuations in the market price of the Company&#8217;s stock.
</B>
	Although the Company has reported profitability in all four quarters of 2015, 2014, 2013 and 2012, the third quarter of 2011 and in 17 consecutive quarters starting from the fourth quarter of 2006, we have also reported losses in the first, second and fourth quarters of 2011. Despite the previously mentioned profitable results, the uncertainty and volatility in current financial markets can result in wide fluctuations in the market price of our stock. The Company&#8217;s operating results have varied on a quarterly basis in the past and may fluctuate significantly in the future.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
<U>
	RISKS ASSOCIATED WITH FOREIGN EXCHANGE
</U>
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	The Company&#8217;s operations are heavily exposed to fluctuations in foreign currencies.
</B>
	Most of the Company&#8217;s sales are denominated in U.S. dollars, Canadian dollars and Great British pounds (GBP). While the Company expects its revenues and expenses will continue to be denominated primarily in U.S. dollars, a portion of its revenues and expenses may be denominated in other foreign currencies in the future. As the functional currency is U.S. dollars, the Company could experience and has experienced the risks of fluctuating currencies. A weaker Canadian dollar decreases operating expenses on conversion to the U.S. dollar. From time to time the Company may choose to engage in currency hedging activities, which may be unsuccessful and expensive.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	A 9% (2014 &#8211; 5%) strengthening/(weakening) in the US$ against the Cdn$ would result in a loss/(gain) in net earnings and a decrease/(increase) in the net financial assets of approximately $38,000 (2014 - $65,000).
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	An 8% (2014 &#8211; 6%) strengthening (weakening) in the US$ against the GBP would result in a loss/(gain) in net earnings and a decrease/(increase) in the net financial assets of approximately $19,000 (2014 - $22,000).
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For further information, please refer to note 7 Financial Instruments Risk under the heading &#8220;Currency Risk&#8221; set forth in the Audited Consolidated Financial Statements for the Years Ended December 31, 2015, 2014 and 2013, filed as Exhibit 6.1 to this annual report on Form 20-F.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
<U>
	RISKS ASSOCIATED WITH INTEREST RATES
</U>
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Borrowings under the Company&#8217;s credit facilities bear interest at prime rate plus a margin. If the Company borrows under the credit facilities, it is exposed to interest rate risks due to fluctuations
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	14
</P>
</DIV>
<BR>
<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage15"></A>
<BR>
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_15">
</A>
<BR>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; PADDING-LEFT: 0%; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
	in these rates. A 1% increase in these rates would increase interest expense by approximately $35,000 annually, assuming the Company borrows a maximum of $3.5 million under our credit facilities.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; PADDING-LEFT: 0%; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
	In addition, borrowings under the Company&#8217;s acquisition loan bear interest at LIBOR plus a margin. For the year ended December 31, 2015, the company has fully repaid its loan balance. For further information, please refer to note 7 Financial Instruments Risk under the heading &#8220;Interest rate risk&#8221; set forth in the Audited Consolidated Financial Statements for the Years Ended December 31, 2015, 2014 and 2013, filed as Exhibit 6.1 to this annual report on Form 20-F.
</P>

<LI>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 6%">
	The Company was incorporated in British Columbia, Canada on October 15, 1982 pursuant to the
<I>
	Company Act
</I>
	(British Columbia). Effective September 27, 1989, the Company changed its name to NII Norsat International, Inc. At the Company&#8217;s Annual General Meeting held on June 9, 1999, shareholders passed a special resolution to change the Company&#8217;s name back to Norsat International Inc. Since July 2, 1999, the Company has operated under the name Norsat International Inc. (herein &#8220;Norsat&#8221; or the &#8220;Company&#8221;).
</P>
<LI>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 6%">
	Norsat was incorporated under and continues to operate under the laws of the Province of British Columbia, Canada. The Company is administered from British Columbia. The corporate laws pertinent to Norsat are those of the Province of British Columbia, although it is also subject to the securities legislation of British Columbia, Ontario and the United States.
</P>

	The Federal Court of Appeal ruled that the use of U.S. based DTH systems in Canada contravened the Radio communication Act. Aurora Distributing, a division of Diamond Pacific Inc., the Company&#8217;s consumer products subsidiary, withdrew from the U.S. based DTH receiving market after Norsat settled a lawsuit in which it was a distributor for those systems.

<TD STYLE="BACKGROUND-COLOR: #FFFFFF" BGCOLOR=#A00000 VALIGN=TOP WIDTH="88%" ALIGN=LEFT>
	The Company acquired IMT Comsys, a private company and originally the Satellite Communications Division of MPR Teltech. IMT Comsys&#8217; products included Ka-band VSATs, solid state power amplifiers LNB downconverters. The acquiree also had development contracts with the European and Canadian Space Agencies for Ka-band subscriber terminals.

Through this acquisition, Norsat added digital video broadcast (DVB) hubs to manage the flow of content into and out of the Internet backbone and between subscriber terminals; and a 100 Mbps IP encapsulator to enable end-to-end multimedia broadcast solutions.

<P>
	In August, the Company formally exited the consumer satellite DBS market. The Company discontinued the operations of Norsat America, a distribution business geared towards consumer-oriented, Direct Broadcasting Systems.

<P>

(&#8220;Norsat&#8221;). As of June 29, 2012, STI and STHI were dissolved under the Business Corporation Act (Ontario) and hence, ceased to exist as legal entities. &#8220;Sinclair Technologies&#8221; continues to operate as a division of Norsat.

<TD STYLE="BACKGROUND-COLOR: #FFFFFF" VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
<P>
	Combiners. The ATOM series of BUCs and SSPAs were the most compact, lightweight, and energy efficient transmitters available in the market. The TXC Series Combiners feature improved performance and were designed to allow a number of transmitters to share a single antenna.
</P>
<P>
	As of December 31, 2014, the acquisition loan balance had been paid down to $2.4 million.

<P>
	On January 16, 2015, the Company consolidated its outstanding common shares on the basis of one new common share for every ten existing common shares.
</P>
<P>
	On February 10, 2015, the Company&#8217;s shares of common stock commenced trading on the NYSE MKT. Norsat&#8217;s ticker symbol is &#8220;NSAT&#8221; and its shares ceased trading on the OTC Bulletin Board (&#8220;OTCBB&#8221;) concurrent with the listing of its shares on the NYSE MKT. The Company&#8217;s common shares also continue to trade on the TSX under the symbol &#8220;NII&#8221;.
</P>
<P>
	In Q2 2015, the Company fully repaid the acquisition loan balance. The Company launched several new products including a new, customized version of the SM2600D which is a low profile, multi-band, multi-port antenna platform ideally suited for the transportation market. The Company also launched the new compact ATOM 25 Watt Ku-band BUCs and SSPAs. The ATOM series of BUCs and SSPAs are the most compact, lightweight, and energy efficient transmitters available in the market.
</P>
<P>
	During Q4, 2015, the Company was awarded a $2.7 million contract from a major U.S. military contractor for its Ku-Band and Wideband Global SATCOM (&#8220;WGS&#8221;)-certified X-Band marine VSAT terminals. This demonstrated that the Company&#8217;s continuous investment in research and development (R&amp;D) has yielded innovations that enabled its off-the-shelf terminals to be easily customized for both military and commercial markets worldwide.
</P>

<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	1. Norsat Business and Principal Activities
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Norsat is a leading provider of innovative communication solutions used by government organizations, militaries, transportation, resource and marine industry companies, news organizations, public safety search and rescue operators and others. Our solutions enable the transmission of data, audio and video for remote and challenging applications. Norsat&#8217;s products and services include leading-edge product design and development, production, distribution and infield support and service of fly-away satellite terminals, microwave components, antennas, radio frequency (RF) conditioning products, maritime based satellite terminals and remote network connectivity solutions.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Our common shares are traded on the TSX under the ticker symbol &#8216;NII&#8217; and on the NYSE MKT under the ticker symbol &#8216;NSAT&#8217;. See Item 10B below with respect to Norsat&#8217;s common shares
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	20
</P>

<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
<U>
	Customer concentration
</U>
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For the year ended December 31, 2015, one customer of the Sinclair Technologies operating segment represented 10% of the Company&#8217;s consolidated revenue (2014 - 11%, 2013 - 14%).
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
<U>
	Business Segments
</U>
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Our business currently operates primarily through two business segments: Sinclair Technologies and Satellite Communications.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	(a) Sinclair Technologies Business Segment
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Sinclair Technologies specializes in RF antenna and filter products designed for high performance, reliability and durability in extreme mechanical/electrical environments and weather conditions. Within these two main product lines, we offer over 2,000 distinct products, including base station antennas, mobile/transit antennas, covert antennas, filters, receiver multicouplers, and accessories. Engineers in our Sinclair Technologies segment are experienced in custom designing complete systems based on the customer&#8217;s unique needs. With a strong focus on R&amp;D and continuous product enhancement, we continue to expand our product offerings and improve existing designs to better serve customers.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<U>
	Antennas
</U>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Our Sinclair Technologies segment has developed an exceptionally broad range of antennas, especially in the frequency bands allocated to public safety, air traffic control and land mobile radio applications. Some of these frequencies are currently being &#8220;re-farmed&#8221; or re-allocated to new applications by governing bodies such as the FCC in the U.S. and Industry Canada. This &#8220;re-farming&#8221; of frequencies creates new demand, which we can satisfy through engineering derivative modifications to our existing products. This, in turn, preserves our leadership position in the antenna market.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Our Sinclair Technologies segment also manufactures several lines of omni-directional, yagi and panel dipole antennas covering the 30 MHz to 1900 MHz bands. Our family of collinear omni-
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	21
</P>
</DIV>
<BR>
<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage22"></A>
<BR>
<!--$$/PAGE=-->
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_22">
</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE=" PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	directional antenna has a strong reputation with private mobile radio operators who use these antennas to provide coverage solutions. Sinclair Technologies was instrumental in developing low passive inter-modulation (&#8220;PIM&#8221;) antennas.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<U>
	Filters
</U>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Sinclair Technologies also produces an extensive portfolio of RF filter products used to optimize the performance of antenna systems including cavity filters, transmitter combiners, duplexers, isolators, circulators and receiver multi-couplers. Our filter product line is based on standard cavity and combines resonator technologies, as well as very small high-performance filters, using cross-coupled technology.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<U>
	Radio Frequency Based Communications - Market Profile
</U>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The antenna and filter products supplied by our Sinclair Technologies segment are used primarily by the Land Mobile Radio industry and specifically by the following industry segments:
</P>
<UL>
<LI>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-LEFT: 4%" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Public safety operators, including several police forces, coast guards and navies, and a large set of ambulance and fire dispatch services;
</P>
<LI>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-LEFT: 4%" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Private sector networks including rail, ground and air transportation networks used by natural resource, utility, taxi, trucking, and construction companies, as well as other dedicated network operators. These customers are generally served through an extensive set of dealers specializing in radio systems;
</P>
<LI>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-LEFT: 4%" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Mobile radio, public safety, aviation and heavy transport industries; and
</P>
<LI>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-LEFT: 4%" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Original equipment manufacturers (OEMs).
</P>
</LI>
</UL>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Sinclair Technologies products are well established globally. Operating in the 30 MHz to 1.9 GHz frequency range, Sinclair Technologies antennas and filters are integral components of many wireless communications networks - controlling, enhancing and propagating radio frequency signals associated with these systems. Most Sinclair Technologies products support both voice and data.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<U>
	Competition
</U>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The primary competition for antenna and filter products are PCTEL Inc. (NASDAQ:PCTI) Tel. Kathrein &#8211; Werke KG, Laird PLC (LSE: LRD.L), Bird Technologies Group, EMR Corporation, Axell Wireless, RFI Corporation, COMPROD., dbSpectra and Radio Frequency Systems (RFS).
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	(b) Satellite Communications Business Segment
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Our Satellite Communications segment provides two broad categories of products: satellite terminals and microwave components.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Our Satellite Solutions segment provides a comprehensive portfolio of fly-away satellite terminals and software interfaces designed for easy portability and reliable connectivity in locations where traditional communication infrastructure is insufficient, unreliable, damaged or non-existent.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	In addition it designs, develops and markets receivers, transmitters and power amplifiers that enable the transmission, reception and amplification of signals to and from satellites. Our product portfolio of microwave components includes a comprehensive range of satellite receivers, transmitters, transceivers, SSPAs and other microwave components.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	22
</P>
</DIV>
<BR>
<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage23"></A>
<BR>
<!--$$/PAGE=-->
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_23">
</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE=" PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<U>
	Satellite Terminals
</U>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Our portfolio of portable satellite systems includes:
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The upgraded Norsat GLOBETrekker&#8482; 2.0 is an intelligent, auto-acquire, rapidly deployable fly-away satellite terminal. GLOBETrekker
<SUP>
	TM
</SUP>
	now includes a modular architecture that enables easy component swapping in the field, a simple one-touch interface, elevated electronics for all terrain deployment and a variety of other feature enhancements that improve usability, performance and ruggedness. The terminal is built to military-grade specifications (MIL-STD-810G) and is easily transported via airline checkable packaging. GLOBETrekker&#8482; is ideal for users with mission critical communication requirements such as military, resource, emergency response, and transportation applications.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The Norsat ROVER&#8482; is an ultra-portable fly-away satellite terminal with assisted acquire technology. Easily assembled in a matter of minutes, the ROVER&#8482; is ideal for the rapid deployments of military and other highly mobile operations. The ROVER&#8482; is easily capable of data transfer rates in excess of 12 Mbps, yet is still compact enough to fit into a single backpack.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	SigmaLink&#8482; is a fly-away satellite terminal with antenna sizes up to 2.4m, suitable for longer term deployments, yet portable enough for mobile operations. SigmaLink&#8482; is ideal for use by government and peacekeeping agencies, broadcasters, resource exploration companies, distance education institutions, financial institutions, and large corporations.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Norsat&#8217;s GLOBETrekker&#8482;, Rover&#8482; and SigmaLink&#8482; fly-away terminals offer superior ease of use, ruggedness, and portability compared to competitive offerings. All systems are shipped with LinkControl software, the industry&#8217;s most intuitive and powerful suite of satellite pointing tools. LinkControl seamlessly integrates the various hardware components, automates the process of satellite acquisition, and enables users to pre-configure settings for rapid field deployments.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	We also have available the RANGER - an assisted-acquire micro-sat terminal. The RANGER is a ruggedized, high performance and portable terminal ideal for rapid deployments where portability is essential.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	We also offer a series of SATCOM Baseband Kits. These convenient, all-in-one tool kits can be used for worldwide satellite system field deployments. Baseband kits support a variety of applications and are available in Compact Flyaway Kits, Emergency Communications Kits and Red/Black Gateway Kits. Key features include the ability to provide core office functions while operating in emergency situations, market leading portability, and connectivity support in challenging environments.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Norsat&#8217;s satellite communications for the maritime market includes the COM series, which is a high performance very small aperture terminal solution, designed for military, fisheries, Oil &amp; Gas and other commercial applications.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	In 2015, Norsat announced the launch of the Journey Manpack ultra-portable Ku-Band satellite terminal, which is a 6-segment, carbon fiber portable terminal weighing less than 18 kilograms (40 pounds), including the backpack, ideal for military Special Forces and government applications that require maximum portability and quick set up.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<U>
	Microwave Products
</U>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Our portfolio of microwave components includes:
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	LNB Down Converters, are required by every satellite antenna (or &#8220;dish&#8221;) irrespective of aperture or location. The LNB Down Converter is mounted at the focal point of the dish to convert
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	23
</P>
</DIV>
<BR>
<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage24"></A>
<BR>
<!--$$/PAGE=-->
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_24">
</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE=" PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	incoming microwave signals into electrical signals that are routed to the remote receiver or indoor unit. Reliability is critical for these products as they are used in remote areas around the world.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Satellite transmitters or BUCs convert electrical signals into microwave signals that can be transmitted to an orbiting satellite. A BUC is required to transmit to a satellite for applications such as news gathering, broadband internet access, and broadcasting.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Norsat&#8217;s product offering includes the new ATOM Series BUCs. These BUCs are amongst the smallest, lightest and most energy efficient transmitters available on the market today. The high efficiency ATOM reduces power consumption significantly; delivering overall cost savings over the lifetime of the device.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Norsat is a market leader in microwave products. Through more than three decades of participation in this market, we have developed a reputation for quality, reliability and innovation. We believe that we have the largest market share of any of our competitors in the commercial LNB space.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<U>
	Satellite&#8211;based Communications - Market Profile
</U>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Norsat&#8217;s satellite-based communications business includes satellite terminals and microwave components. These products employ satellites that are orbiting the earth to transmit and receive content. Our equipment interoperates with satellites that orbit the earth at the same speed as the earth rotates. These satellites appear to remain at the same point relative to the earth&#8217;s surface, thus giving the impression that they are stationary. These satellites are known as geostationary satellites, or satellites in geostationary orbit (orbiting approximately 22,300 miles above the earth).
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	While geostationary satellites are operated on a commercial basis and are standard in their operation, some are owned and operated by militaries and may have unique characteristics. Our equipment has been standardized so that it can operate on most satellites, without further customization. These products permit users to establish a broadband communications link (up to 10 Mbps) between any two points on earth. This broadband communications link is capable of transporting a broad range of content including voice, data and motion video.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The satellite industry continues to see increased demand, driven primarily by the backlog of satellite launches, across all sectors of the market including the commercial and military markets. Our products operate primarily on widely deployed commercial Ku-band satellites. However, some of our products operate on other commercial (C-band and Ka-band) and military (Ka-band and X-band) satellites as well.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<U>
	Competition
</U>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For satellite terminals, the Company faces competition from General Dynamics Corp. (NYSE: GD), C3ISR, a segment of L-3 Communications Holdings Inc. (NYSE: LLL), TeleCommunication Systems Inc. (NASDAQ: TSYS), Globecomm Systems Inc. (NASDAQ: GCOM) and Ultra electronics, Gigasat, a segment of Ultra electronics Holdings PLC (LSE: ULE). From time to time, the Company also faces competition from Swe-Dish, a subsidiary of Rockwell Collins (NYSE: COL). At times, the Company also faces competition from systems integrators who construct systems on a custom basis for the military including Airbus Group (Euronext: EAD), Lockheed Martin (NYSE: LMT) and Raytheon Company (NYSE: RTN).
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	In the broadcast and commercial markets, the Company faces competition from terrestrial alternatives such as microwave radio vendors and the traditional providers of portable satellite systems including: Swe-Dish, a subsidiary of Rockwell Collins (NYSW: COL); VisLink Plc&#8217;s Advent business unit; Ultra electronics, Gigasat and Holkirk Communications, a subsidiary of Sematron (UK) Ltd. The Company also faces competition from service providers such as Harris
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	24
</P>
</DIV>
<BR>
<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage25"></A>
<BR>
<!--$$/PAGE=-->
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_25">
</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE="PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Caprock Communications and Spacenet, a subsidiary of Gilat Satellite Networks Ltd. (NYSE:GILT).
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For microwave products, the primary competition for this business unit comes from New Japan Radio Co, Ltd (Tokyo Stock Exchange: 6911) and to a lesser extent from the Company&#8217;s own suppliers. The Company also faces competition in the BUCs market from Wavestream, a subsidiary of Gilat Satellite Networks Ltd. (NASDAQ: GILT).
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	2. Marketing
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The Company sells most of its microwave components and portable satellite, other than those bound for the U.S. government, through resellers. Almost all of the portable satellite systems sold to the U.S. government have been through the Company&#8217;s direct sales force.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Norsat also sells antenna and radio frequency conditioning products to approximately 1,800 distinct customers. The Company markets these products in North America through a direct sales force, OEMs, distributors and manufacturer representatives. In Europe, Middle East and Africa, the Company&#8217;s products are sold through a direct sales force, OEMs, and system integrators. The Company will continue to use these sales channels and pursue opportunities to cross-sell these products to customers within all of the Company&#8217;s divisions.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The Company&#8217;s primary value proposition is rooted in its longevity and reputation for quality. Customers with critical applications tend to place significant value in the quality of Norsat products and the after-sales support infrastructure.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	3
</B>
<B>
<I>
	.
</I>
</B>
<B>
	Research and Development
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	R&amp;D activities and projects are focused on developing new products in the different business segments the Company is involved in. The Company spent 8% of its annual revenues excluding any government contributions and allocated 16% of its staff towards R&amp;D activities.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	4. Intellectual Property
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The Company relies on patent, trademark, trade secret and copyright laws to protect our proprietary technology and to protect us against claims from others. The Company believes it has direct intellectual property rights covering substantially all of its material technologies. However, there can be no assurance that claims of infringement will not be asserted against the Company or against its customers in connection with their use of its systems and products, nor can there be any assurance as to the outcome of any such claims, given the technological complexity of the Company&#8217;s systems and products.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The Company has renewed interest in employing patent protection due to competition in its markets. The Company has a patent portfolio of four patents. The Company does not believe that any single patent is material to its business as a whole.
</P>

<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
	Description of Property
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The Company's head office and principal place of business has been located in Richmond, British Columbia, Canada since September 2006. The Company leases its head office premises.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The lease is for approximately 30,400 square feet of space. This location houses the Company's corporate office, engineering and production department and includes warehouse space.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The Company has leased premises in Aurora, Ontario, Canada. The lease is for approximately 45,246 square feet of space. This location houses the antenna and radio frequency conditioning product sales office, engineering and production department. It also includes warehouse space.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Most of the Company&#8217;s products are produced and shipped out of the Richmond and Aurora locations.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Norsat also operates out of leased premises in Lincoln and Somersham, England; and Hamburg, New York.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	There are no known environmental issues that may affect the Company&#8217;s utilization of its assets at any of the above locations.
</P>

<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage29"></A>
<BR>
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_4">
</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE="PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Results from our two revenue generating business segments fluctuate from quarter-to-quarter due to seasonal influences on sales volumes. In our Sinclair Technologies segment, the first and second quarters are historically the strongest, as most of Sinclair Technologies&#8217; customers build inventories during these quarters prior to commencing installation in the spring and summer seasons. For our Satellite Communications segment, the third and fourth quarters are typically the strongest, as these have traditionally been the periods when military sales occur. The timing of contract awards also creates significant fluctuations in our quarterly results as some large contracts represent a significant share of sales for a given quarter. The timing of these orders is unpredictable.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	We are working to reduce quarterly revenue fluctuations by cultivating revenue streams that are more stable in nature and distributed throughout the year. Our acquisition of Sinclair Technologies reflects this strategy as Sinclair Technologies&#8217; sales are generally more evenly distributed than those of our other segments. They also tend to be strongest during periods when sales from the Satellite Communication segment are relatively weak. We have mitigated revenue instability by creating revenue backlog, which is expected to help reduce some of the volatility in our financial results in 2016.
</P>

<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
	Fiscal 2015 Compared to Fiscal 2014
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For the year ended December 31, 2015, Norsat recorded total sales of $36.1 million, consistent with total sales of $36.2 million in 2014.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Sinclair Technologies sales were $18.8 million in 2015, compared to $21.7 million in 2014. Sales from this segment were impacted by the continued softness in the infrastructure and public safety markets as a result of the current economic conditions, especially in Canada.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Satellite Communications sales were $17.3 million in 2015 compared to $14.5 million in 2014. Satellite terminal sales were $8.2 million, compared to $2.8 million in 2014, reflecting stronger satellite terminal sales to commercial customers in addition to the existing military market. Microwave Products sales were $9.1 million in 2015 compared to $11.7 million in 2014. The $2.6 million decrease was mainly due to the deliveries against a significant ATOM product contract in 2014, which was not repeated in 2015.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	29
</P>
</DIV>
<BR>
<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage30"></A>
<BR>
<!--$$/PAGE=-->
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_5">
</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE="PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	On a consolidated basis, gross profit was $14.6 million or 41% in 2015 compared to $14.4 million or 40% in 2014. Sinclair Technologies&#8217; gross profit margin percentage in 2015 increased to 46% from 40% in 2014, as a result of the strengthening of the U.S. dollar against the Canadian dollar as our labor, overhead costs and certain material costs were incurred in Canadian dollars. Gross profit margins from the Satellite Communications segment were 35% in 2015, compared to 40% in 2014, which reflected lower margin revenue in the product mix and competitive price pressures.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
	Fiscal 2014 Compared to Fiscal 2013
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For the year ended December 31, 2014, Norsat recorded total sales of $36.2 million, down slightly compared to $36.4 million in 2013.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Sinclair Technologies sales were $21.7 million, compared to $22.5 million in 2013. The year-over-year decrease in revenues reflected softness in the infrastructure and public safety markets.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Satellite Communications sales were $14.5 million in 2014 compared to $13.9 million in 2013. Satellite terminal sales were $2.8 million in 2014, compared to $4.8 million in 2013. Sales from this segment were impacted by reduced military ordering of satellite equipment and services. In addition, service revenues declined to $0.7 million compared to $2.3 million as airtime, warranties and post-service contracts expired. Microwave Products sales were $11.7 million in 2014, compared to $9.1 million in 2013. The $2.6 million increase was mainly driven by the product deliveries on the ATOM new line of products.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	On a consolidated basis, gross profit was $14.4 million or 40% in 2014 compared to $13.8 million or 38% in 2013. Sinclair Technologies gross profit margin percentage was 40% in 2014, compared to 43% in 2013. The decrease in gross margin was due to increase in labor and overheads costs in 2014. Gross profit margins from the Satellite Communications segment were 40% in 2014, compared to 30% in 2013, reflecting a decrease in inventory write-off of $0.5 million in 2014, compared to $1.2 million in 2013 and higher margin products in the sales mix in 2014.
</P>

<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
	Fiscal 2015 Compared to Fiscal 2014
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For the year ended December 31, 2015, total expenses were $9.9 million, compared to $10.7 million in 2014.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Selling and distributing expenses decreased to $4.9 million in 2015, from $5.4 million in 2014, reflecting the strengthening of the U.S. dollar against the Canadian dollar, as a significant portion of the Company&#8217;s selling and distribution expenses were incurred in Canadian dollars. In addition, commission expenses were lower in Sinclair Technologies in 2015 due to the decrease in sales but were partially offset by higher commission expenses in the Satellite Communications segment due to the increase in sales in that segment.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	General and administrative expenses increased to $4.1 million in 2015, from $4.0 million in 2014. The increase reflected investments in organizational infrastructure, increased bonus due to the Company substantially tracking towards its 2015 targets and objectives, and offset by the strengthening of the U.S. dollar against the Canadian dollar as a significant portion of the Company&#8217;s administration expenses were incurred in Canadian dollars.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For the year ended December 31, 2015, direct product development expenses increased to $2.9 million from $2.8 million for 2014. The increase headcount in product development was partially offset by the strengthening of the U.S. dollar against the Canadian dollar as a significant portion of the Company&#8217;s product development expenses were incurred in Canadian dollars.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Government contributions were $1.3 million for the year ended December 31, 2015, consistent with $1.3 million in 2014.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	As a result net product development expenses were $1.6 million for the year ended December 31, 2015, consistent with $1.6 million in 2014.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Gain on foreign exchange for the year ended December 31, 2015 was $0.8 million, compared to $0.6 million gain for 2014.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Interest expense was reduced to $0.1 million for the year ended December 31, 2015 from $0.2 million for 2014 due to the repayment of the remaining balance of the acquisition loan in Q2 2015.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
	Fiscal 2014 Compared to Fiscal 2013
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For the year ended December 31, 2014, total expenses were $10.7 million, compared to $10.8 million in 2013.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Selling and distributing expenses decreased to $5.4 million in 2014, from $6.3 million in 2013, reflecting the strengthening of the U.S. dollar against the Canadian dollar, as a significant portion of the Company&#8217;s expenses were incurred in Canadian Dollars, and employee-related costs savings.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	31
</P>
</DIV>

<HR STYLE="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER SIZE=1 WIDTH="100%" NOSHADE>
<A NAME="eolPage32"></A>
<BR>
<A NAME="NORSATINTL20F_HTM_PAGE_7">
</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE="PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	General and administrative expenses increased to $4.0 million in 2014, from $3.7 million in 2013. In 2014, corporate development costs related to external costs to pursue a potential acquisition increased to $0.2 million compared to $0.1 million in 2013. In addition, investments were made in organizational infrastructure and bonuses increased due to the Company substantially achieving its 2014 targets and objectives. These increases were offset by the decrease in expenses, reflecting the strengthening of the U.S. dollar against the Canadian dollar, as a significant portion of the Company&#8217;s expenses were incurred in Canadian dollars.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For the year ended December 31, 2014, direct product development expenses decreased to $2.8 million from $3.5 million for 2013. The decrease reflected the accelerated development of the newly acquired CVG product lines in 2013, costs not incurred in 2014, and the impact of the strengthening of the U.S. dollar against the Canadian dollar, as a significant portion of the Company&#8217;s expenses were incurred in Canadian Dollars, and employee-related costs savings.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Government contributions decreased to $1.3 million for the year ended December 31, 2014 from $2.1 million in 2013. In 2013, we secured a new repayable government contribution under the SADI program, which enabled the Company to claim eligible costs incurred starting from July 27, 2012 up to and including December 31, 2017. As a result of the timing of the award, a larger portion of the government contributions were recorded in 2013 to capture the contributions related to the eligible expenses incurred in 2012 and 2013.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	As a result net product development expenses increased to $1.6 million for the year ended December 31, 2014 from $1.4 million in 2013.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Gain on foreign exchange for the year ended December 31, 2014 was $0.6 million, compared to $0.9 million gain for 2013.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Interest expense was reduced to $0.2 million for the year ended December 31, 2014 from $0.3 million for 2013 due to the repayments made towards the acquisition loan during 2014.
</P>

<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
	Fiscal 2015 Compared to Fiscal 2014
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Earnings before income taxes for the year ended December 31, 2015 increased to $4.8 million, from $3.7 million in 2014.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	The increase was mainly as a result of an increase of gross margin of $0.3 million and a decrease of total expenses by $0.8 million. The increase in gross margin and decrease in operating costs primarily reflected the strengthening of the U.S. dollar against the Canadian dollar as our labor, overhead and operating costs were incurred in Canadian dollars.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Net income tax recovery for the year ended December 31, 2015 was $3.9 million compared to $0.5 million for 2014. This reflected a current income tax recovery of approximately $66,000 for the year ended December 31, 2015 compared to $0.2 million in 2014 and a deferred income tax recovery of $3.8 million for the year ended December 31, 2015 compared to $0.3 million in 2014. During the fourth quarter of 2015, we assessed the Company&#8217;s ability to realize deferred income
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	32
</P>
</DIV>
<BR>

</A>
<BR>
<DIV STYLE=" PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	tax assets and based on our history of profitability in our Canadian operations, we concluded that it was probable an additional $3.8 million of deferred income tax assets and investment tax credits recoverable will be utilized against estimated future taxable income.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For the year ended December 31, 2015, net earnings increased to $8.7 million, or $1.50 per share, basic and diluted, from net earnings of $4.2 million, or $0.73 per share, basic and diluted, for 2014.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
	Fiscal 2014 Compared to Fiscal 2013
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Earnings before income taxes for the year ending December 31, 2014 increased to $3.7 million, from $3.0 million in 2013, reflecting a $0.6 million higher gross profit, $0.4 million lower net expenses, and $0.1 million lower interest charges compared to 2013. This was offset by a lower gain on foreign exchange for the year ended December 31, 2014 compared to 2013.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Income tax recovery for the year ended December 31, 2014 was $0.5 million compared to $0.7 million for 2013, reflecting a current income tax recovery of $0.2 million for the year ended December 31, 2014 compared to a current tax expense of $0.3 million in 2013. Deferred income tax recovery was $0.3 million for the year ended December 31, 2014, compared to a deferred income tax recovery of $1.0 million in 2013.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For the year ended December 31, 2014, net earnings increased to $4.2 million, or $0.73 per share, basic and diluted, from net earnings of $3.7 million, or $0.64 per share, basic and diluted, for 2013.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
<U>
	Outlook
</U>
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	For fiscal 2016, the Company has had a positive start and has continued shipments on a significant Satellite Communications sale contract. The Company also continues to have good quoting activities.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Looking longer-term, the Company continues to invest in R&amp;D to diversify its business by broadening its product portfolio and expanding its customer base on a geographic and market sector basis. Norsat continues to focus on markets beyond the U.S., as well as on the commercial, resource, transportation and public safety segments. The Company is also continuing to pursue other new revenue opportunities both organically and through acquisitions.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Despite the current global economic uncertainties, Norsat continues to generate profits and strong cash flow. This stability has created a strong financial position and capital structure, and will enable management to continue to create excellent conditions for realizing additional growth opportunities through business combinations. The Company will continue to actively pursue merger and acquisition opportunities that provide strong value, further key strategic objectives and have the potential to be accretive to shareholders. In the interim, the Company&#8217;s cash position should continue to remain strong.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
	Management will also continue to execute a balanced growth strategy that incorporates investment in staffing level, new product introductions, continued enhancement of existing product lines, greater diversification by geographic regions as well as by industry verticals, and a broadening of the solutions we provide to customers. In addition, the Company continues to evaluate other strategic opportunities for improving overall operating and financial performance.
</P>
<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: RIGHT">
	33
</P>
</DIV>

<P STYLE="TEXT-ALIGN: JUSTIFY; MARGIN-LEFT: 4%">
<B>
<I>
<U>
	Critical Accounting Estimates

</B>
